Chamber of Commerce Petitions the City Government: Do Not Detain Minor Offenses 118

Improve Bureaucratic Bad Habits, Hoping to Avoid Wasting Time

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce submitted a petition to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating, "Regarding the matter of petitioning: On the 18th of this month, the Flower and Tree Industry, Southern Goods Industry, Sand and Stone Industry, Steel Bar and Old Iron Industry, Sandalwood and Longan Store Industry, Bamboo Industry, Sandboat Trade, and other trade associations jointly sent a letter stating that citizens in the city each have their own business. If they encounter minor matters that require interrogation by the public security bureau in each district, minor cases that are not important can be resolved if they are interrogated immediately. However, the district bureaus do not care whether the case is minor or major, and often order the parties involved, both plaintiff and defendant, to be detained in the district bureau from morning till night before interrogating them. This situation may be acceptable for major cases, but applying it to minor cases inevitably wastes other people's time and disregards people's livelihoods. At a time when the New Life Movement is being promoted, these bureaucratic bad habits should be improved. Minor offenses should be handled quickly to avoid citizens aimlessly waiting, wasting time, and hindering the freedom of business. For this reason, it is suggested that the Public Security Bureau be instructed to order each district bureau to seek speed in handling cases in the future. In the event of major cases, the plaintiff may be allowed to provide a guarantee to appear when summoned, and the plaintiff should not be detained in the district bureau at the same time. After reviewing the case files, it was found that in criminal cases where the circumstances are not very serious and there is no risk of flight, bail may be legally allowed to avoid detention. As for plaintiffs who are self-represented, there is no system for adding detention. Criminal cases are still ongoing, not to mention the handling of district bureaus, most of which are minor offenses, which should be interrogated immediately. If there are too many cases to interrogate, they can be summoned again the next day, so why detain them first? It is clear that this is an illegal deprivation of people's freedom. This matter, combined with the statements of the trade associations, shows that it is a long-standing habit that is not a matter of a day or two. It is necessary for your government to explain the importance of respecting the rule of law and order them to abolish these bad habits and properly establish legal procedures. If any district bureaus still detain people in minor offense cases in the future, they should be dismissed and investigated at any time to ensure the rule of law and discipline officials. It is therefore reasonable to submit this petition to your government for review and approval for implementation, which would be in the public interest."

Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on Smokers, Convenes Senior Police for Instructions 119

Seventy or Eighty People Arrested in the Old North Gate Area Yesterday

The Municipal Public Security Bureau has been conducting registration of smokers for more than a month. The deadline for renewing the second-term licenses is also at the end of this month. Fearing that some smokers may still be missed, the bureau has recently dispatched police officers to intensify the crackdown efforts. All procedures are more stringent than before. The area around the Old North Gate in South Shanghai is an area where many smokers live, and the bureau pays special attention to it. Yesterday, Dai, the section chief of the bureau's Fourth Section, led all investigators to the Old North Gate Police Station, convened all patrol officers and police chiefs for instructions, and instructed on how to investigate smokers who had delayed renewing their licenses and those who had not registered. After the instructions, the investigators and police chiefs from the station were mixed and divided into groups to carry out the inspection. It is reported that as many as seventy or eighty smokers were arrested.

Rumor: Chen Zhongfu Passes Through Shanghai to Japan 121

The Ryuta Maru Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday, but Could Not Be Found

A Passenger Suspected, but His Entourage Denied It

The Xin Sheng News Agency reported that Chen Zhongfu, the former Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, returned to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee in Guangdong after resigning to serve as a diplomatic liaison in the Southwest. A Hong Kong telegram reported that Chen passed through Hong Kong from Guangdong on the 17th, taking the Japanese postal ship Ryuta Maru to Shanghai en route to Japan. The ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday at 1:30 PM (one hour late according to the original schedule) and docked at the Yangshupu Huishan Wharf. It is scheduled to leave Shanghai for Japan at 8:30 AM this morning. A Xin Sheng News Agency reporter boarded the ship yesterday but could not find Chen. Only a passenger named Chen was found in room 267. When the reporter knocked on the door and entered, he saw someone who appeared to be an attendant speaking with a Cantonese accent. That person said that the master was indeed named Chen and had gone out. He was traveling to Kobe, but denied that he was Chen Zhongfu.

China International Famine Relief Commission: Dredging of Quan River in Shandong Province Completed 130

The Quan River is located in the territory of Wenshang County, Shandong Province. Recently, due to the narrow and shallow river channel, it has often suffered from flooding, especially last year. The China International Famine Relief Commission, located at 505 Henan Road in this city, in order to provide relief to the victims, issued 15,500 yuan in national currency and 1,000 bags of flour to carry out work relief and engage in dredging. Since work began on March 24th of this year, a total of 1,550 workers have been hired. Because the mud volume counting system was used, with wages based on the cubic measure of mud dug, the workers were very diligent. The project progressed very quickly and was completed on the 6th of this month. From now on, 160,000 acres of farmland, 170 villages, and 40,000 residents along the river can avoid flooding. It is reported that in addition to a living expense of 11 cents, each worker in this work relief project can earn 15 to 20 cents per day, which can be used to support their families, leaving an average of 10 cents per day.

Shantytown Residents in Zhabei Petitioned the Party and Government Yesterday 131

Due to Forced Eviction Orders from Nearby Police Stations

The Authorities Granted a Stay of Eviction and Will Investigate the Truth

Residents of shantytowns at the intersections of Changan, Yutong, and Tongji Roads in Zhabei District of this city were recently ordered to relocate by the Hengfeng Road Police Station, with a one-week deadline. The shantytown residents were shocked and terrified upon hearing this. They immediately elected Peng Yuanfeng, Liu Dongshan, Liu Zhaocai, Dong Xueshi, Cai Zhucheng, Miao Xiangben, Bu Shunchang, Yu Zuofa, Sun Langhong, Zheng Kaiju, and others as their authorized representatives. Yesterday, around 1 p.m., they led over a hundred men, women, children, and elderly people to the Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, Social Affairs Bureau, and Public Security Bureau to appeal and deliver petition letters. Representatives from each government agency met with them and agreed to their requests. In addition to immediately ordering the police station to postpone the forced eviction, they also dispatched personnel to investigate the truth. The representatives were satisfied and then left. The petition letter from the shantytown representatives is transcribed below, regarding the excessive oppression and harsh eviction deadlines that are pushing over a thousand residents to their deaths. Please provide swift relief to alleviate their suffering. The shantytown residents previously appealed to the Hengfeng Road Police Station chief (unnamed) because he repeatedly sent police officers to their doors to order the demolition of their houses, dismantling beams and pulling down walls, causing great disturbance. Following an unfortunate incident of arson, the shantytown residents requested that your (department/government/bureau) convene thorough negotiations with the landlord, Gu Lanji (meetings held on February 15th and March 16th), and separately sent letters requesting direct discussions with the landlord (letters dated February 24th and March 11th). They also petitioned the Public Security Bureau. All of these actions have proof of receipt. The shantytown residents were quietly waiting for a resolution. Before your (department/government/bureau) could convene local authorities, the police chief suddenly issued a notice on the 11th of this month (photo attached), stating that the shantytown residents were occupying the land and obstructing other people's construction, and under the guise of cleaning up the city, ordered the shantytown residents to move out voluntarily within one week from the date of the notice. He also ordered police officers to forcibly evict them, even more harshly than before. Chief Lu summoned shantytown representatives Peng Yuanxiang, Miao Xiangben, Cai Zhucheng, and Yu Zuofa to the police station three times, severely reprimanding them and exerting his power to the fullest extent. The shantytown residents are all victims of disasters from various regions and bankrupt farmers who have no place to return. Moving to public civilian villages is not an option for the shantytowns due to difficulties in paying rent, finding shopkeepers to act as guarantors, and hindering their ability to find work. Moreover, the existing new villages are already full. If forced eviction proceeds, the shantytown residents will suffer from exposure to the elements, affecting their livelihoods, and the old and weak will perish in ditches, while the young and strong will resort to desperate measures. It is feared that instead of improving the city's appearance, it will affect social order. Furthermore, considering the thatched huts near Chief Lu's jurisdiction, there are no less than a hundred places, and some are closer and more relevant. Chief Lu does not prioritize those first, which shows his unfairness. Moreover, during this economic downturn, landlords in Shanghai are wary of building houses. Even if Gu Lanji needs the land for construction, the shantytown residents have requested negotiations multiple times, but they have been rejected. If there is an act of occupation, what legal protection is there? It is suspected that Chief Lu is acting as an accomplice and is oppressing the poor because there are unspeakable hidden motives. We further request that you investigate past construction on the land, including the design, purchase of materials, employment of labor, contracts, and other procedures. This will prove that the landlord is not really needing the land for construction and that some people are profiting from this situation. The shantytown residents' lives are at stake, and they are unwilling to be exploited by a few profiteers. Therefore, with tears, they implore your (department/government/bureau) to uphold your consistent principle of loving the people, promptly summon the local Gu Lanji and the shantytown residents to your (department/government/bureau) for face-to-face discussions to find a thorough solution. Send a letter to the Public Security Bureau, ordering Chief Lu to wait for a resolution and refrain from oppression, to alleviate the suffering and ensure social stability, which would be both a public service and a benefit.

Good News for Those Suffering from Heart Disease 134

Progress in Electric Heart Testing

Diagnosis with Automatic Current Photography

In recent years, the number of Chinese people suffering from heart and vascular diseases has been increasing. Recently, Chairman Hu Zhentang also died from a circulatory disease. Dr. Ding Hui, MD and Lu Yihou, MD, recognizing the increasing severity of heart disease patients and the difficulty of diagnosis, visited renowned cardiology research institutes in Bad Nauheim, Germany, last spring, with the official mandate to study new medical technologies in Europe and America. They conducted an in-depth study of the latest electric cardiac automatic testing machine for researching heart disease. When a person's body is at rest, only the heart function generates activity. Current is introduced at both ends of the body and amplified. Any disturbances in the heart's stimulation function and the nerve conduction regulations can be captured using this automatic test to obtain a film photograph for accurate diagnosis. All circulatory diseases, such as arteriosclerosis, high blood pressure, or heart failure caused by kidney disease, diabetes, acute infectious diseases, lung disease, and opium addiction, can be diagnosed and treated using this machine to determine the course of the disease. It is truly good news for heart disease patients.

Medical Doctor Chen Kehui, PhD, Returned to China from the United States 136

Invented Western Medicine with Chinese Herbs Abroad

Dr. Chen Kehui, PhD, graduated from Tsinghua University at a young age with excellent grades. He was recommended by the university to study in the United States, where he graduated from the University of Wisconsin and Johns Hopkins University, earning a doctoral degree. He has conducted in-depth research on Chinese medicine and has invented various effective medicines by extracting from Chinese herbs, gaining fame in Europe and America. His most notable invention is Ephedrine (Ephedking), extracted from ephedra, which is specifically used to treat asthma and is highly effective. People from various countries admire it. Chen is the first person internationally to produce Western medicine from Chinese medicine, selling it in Europe and America, and becoming world-renowned. People in Europe and America now have a deeper understanding of Chinese medicine, thanks to Chen. Chen served as the director of the pharmaceutical department at Lioly Pharmaceutical Company in the United States for many years. Now, having been away from his homeland for a long time, he feels a strong longing for home. Therefore, he embarked on the President Jackson from the United States on the 16th of this month to return home to visit his family. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai around the 7th of next month. Chen's ancestral home is Qingpu, and he is the brother of Chen Kecheng, the current Secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Government and Director of the News Censorship Bureau. At that time, friends in Shanghai will welcome him.

Austrian Automobile Travelers Arrive in Shanghai 137

Ress and Hallmann

According to the "North China Daily News," Austrian automobile travelers Ress and Hallmann, both from Vienna, departed from Vienna by car a year ago, intending to reach Shanghai in the shortest possible time. They traveled through good, bad, and nearly impassable roads, covering a total of 16,800 miles, and have now safely arrived in Shanghai. They now intend to return to their country by ship. They spent four months traveling through Palestine, Iraq, Persia, Afghanistan, Baluchistan, and India to Calcutta, covering approximately 9,000 miles. According to an interview with the "North China Daily News" yesterday (the 18th), this section of the journey was the safest of the entire trip. There were only one or two difficult spots in Afghanistan. Both believe that within a few years, traveling by car from India to Europe will be common. Most travelers circumnavigating the world ship their cars from Singapore to Saigon or another port in Vietnam. However, Ress and Hallmann claim to be the first to avoid this difficulty. They crossed the north of Indochina and the Quas and Annam provinces of Vietnam. They showed a document signed by a high-ranking official of the Vietnamese government as proof. However, that section of the journey was the most difficult. Trapped in dense forests with no roads, they were delayed and could only cover 120 miles. They needed the help of 30 coolies and spent a month and a half to complete it. In Quas, they had to disassemble the car to cross the strong currents of the Mekong River. They were grateful for the valuable assistance provided by the local chieftains. After traveling in China, they will forever have pleasant memories in their hearts. They were impressed by the progress of road construction in China. They entered China from Indochina, passing through Nanning, Guilin, and entering Hunan Province. The highway on the border of Guizhou and Hunan has not yet been completed, but with the assistance of local officials, they were able to cross the rice fields. Then they entered Jiangxi Province, touring Jingdezhen. They then took the route through Anhui and Zhejiang to reach Shanghai. The purpose of this long journey by car was to let the world know that there is a place called Austria, and they plan to bring back many films of scenic spots and report their experiences to the Austrian Travel Club. The car driven by one of them is novel in design, with larger wheels than ordinary ones, so that it can avoid getting stuck in mud and drive on rough roads. The car body is specially made for long-distance travelers. The oil tank can hold enough gasoline to travel 600 miles, and there is also a water tank that stores 18 gallons of water. This is Ress's third trip of this nature. In 1932, he traveled through the Sahara Desert, and from 1933 to 1934, he traveled from Europe to India, covering 8,000 miles. The two now plan to stay in Shanghai for about a week, then return to Vienna via the Suez Canal.

Mr. Wheelock, a British national and a well-known tea merchant in Shanghai, had been doing business in China for over thirty years. He had served as a director and deputy chairman of the Municipal Council. Wheelock recently passed away in England on the 15th of this month at the age of ninety-two. Wheelock came to China in 1864 and left in 1900 to return to England. It is said that the Chairman of the Municipal Council, Arnold, has sent a letter to his son to express his condolences.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Executive Committee Member's Bribery Case: Zheng Chengqing Flees in Fear of Punishment, Zhang Bofang Sentenced to Two Years and Six Months 140

With a fine of 500 yuan and deprivation of public rights for five years. Bail granted during appeal period.

Zheng Chengqing, an Executive Committee member of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, fabricated a dispatch order in the name of Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, falsely claiming that the Party and National flags manufactured by the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company used Japanese materials. He instructed Zhang Bofang to take the document to the company's General Manager, Zhang Rongchu, to intimidate and extort money. Zhang Rongchu reported the incident to the Chamber of Commerce, which investigated and verified the facts. The Chamber of Commerce resolved to revoke Zheng's position as an Executive Committee member, and Yu Zuoting, on behalf of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, filed a criminal lawsuit with the First Special District Court against Zheng and Zhang for forgery, intimidation, extortion, and damage to reputation. Zheng Chengqing, knowing that he could not escape punishment, fled before the court could detain him and has now been wanted. Zhang Bofang claimed that he was deceived by Zheng at the time, so he obeyed the summons and was taken into custody. He was released on bail of 10,000 yuan. The public trial of the case was held yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. Zhang, accompanied by his defense lawyer Fan Gang, appeared in court. Judge Jiang Shuzi ascended the first court, inquired about Zhang's age, occupation, and address, and then announced the verdict. The main text of the judgment stated that Zhang Bofang was sentenced to two years and six months imprisonment for attempted extortion, with a fine of 500 yuan and deprivation of public rights for five years. If the fine is converted to forced labor, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. Other charges were dismissed. After reciting the judgment, Judge Jiang briefly explained the reasons for the conviction to the defendant in court, stating that the plaintiff had accused the defendant of three crimes. After investigation, it was determined that the purpose of using the forged private document was to intimidate and extort money. Therefore, the two crimes were related. Although the extortion was unsuccessful, the act of committing continuous crimes could not be denied. According to the law, both crimes were combined and the heavier punishment was applied. Regarding the charge of damaging reputation, the forged document was not publicly disseminated, so it was dismissed. If the defendant was not satisfied with the judgment, he could appeal according to the law. Lawyer Fan requested that the defendant be allowed to continue bail during the appeal period. Judge Jiang immediately ruled that the original bail would be granted. The bribery case involving the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Executive Committee member, which had caused a sensation, came to a temporary end.

Zhou Baocai, the Main Suspect in the Assassination of Song Xihou, Has Been Arrested 141

Zhou used to be a clerk in the Hergling Company and had a commission dispute of 500 taels with Song. However, I believe that he instigated the murder of Song. He resided at No. 10, Sida Village, Lane 142, Remi Road, French Concession. Song Xihou, a compradore of the Shanghai office of the British Hergling Company, a cotton yarn merchant, was suddenly visited by two thugs wearing suits and speaking with a northern accent on the morning of the 8th of this month at 11:20 a.m., claiming to be delivering a letter.

Under the Pretense of Visiting Song

They shot Song and his maid Du Chen, seriously wounding them. They died after ineffective medical treatment. Song's concubine Shao and another maid Yuan Xu were also shot and injured and are now being treated at Renji Hospital. The French Police Department has ordered the arrest of the murderers. All details have been reported in this newspaper. Zhou Buguang, the chief detective of the French Police Department, received a tip-off on the 18th and, together with Deputy Detective Qin Youyu and detectives Tao Ronglin and Dai Rongji, waited at the intersection of Dongxinqiao Street and Ningbo Road at 2 p.m. that afternoon and arrested Zhou Binyi Cai (also known as Chunfeng, 48 years old), a native of Ningbo and a major suspect in this case. He was taken to the police station. Zhou confessed that he lived at No. 10, Bing'an Lane, Elaige Road, Zhujiaqiao. He used to be a clerk at the Hergling Company. After the company closed, he worked as an accountant in the tea hall for the female entertainers at the Guangming Theater in the New World Amusement Park. Yesterday, he was escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 District Court, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the interrogation. Lawyer Yuan Jiahuang of the Police Department stated the case, saying that the defendant was arrested for

Inciting Murder

The Police Department is still conducting a detailed investigation and requested a postponement to investigate the matter before formally prosecuting it. Detective Tao Ronglin then reported that the defendant had been a clerk when the victim Song Xihou's father was a compradore at the Hergling Company, until Song Xihou took over and the company closed down. It was found that the defendant and Song Xihou had previously colluded in the sale of machinery with a commission of 5,000 to 6,000 taels, and the defendant was entitled to 500 taels. However, when the company closed, this amount had not been obtained. The defendant often went to Song's house to demand it. Song agreed to give him 400 yuan, but later refused to pay it because the defendant spoke badly. The defendant also went to Song's new residence in Sida Village to demand the money.

At the Time of Song's Murder

The two assailants in suits said to Song, "Why haven't you paid me the 400 yuan? I'm going to kill you." The letter held by the assailants was signed and stamped by Xu Qianlin, a well-respected figure in Shanghai, and it was Xu's stationery. After inquiring with Xu, the stationery and seal matched Xu's, but I believe that the letter must have been forged by someone else. When the assailants entered Song's back door, they told the maid that Mr. Xu had a letter and wanted to see Mr. Song about buying machinery. After investigation, various clues suggest that the defendant is related. The interrogation revealed that defendant Zhou Baocai admitted that he did indeed have a commission dispute of 500 taels with Song, but denied instigating the murder of Song. The court approved a postponement to investigate the case further. The defendant was taken back into custody.

A lawyer appeared in court, stating that the Shanghai Mental Hospital run by Gu was in arrears of more than 3,000 yuan in rent and had been sued by the landlord, Ma Hongkui. Qian Zhongdao Sued for Embezzlement and Breach of Trust; Clarification Based on Facts 143

Mutual Understanding Regarding the Recovery of Stocks

Hearing Adjourned for Ten Days Pending Further Interrogation and Debate. The legal representative (liquidator) of the Zhengda Bank Liquidation Office (lawyer Wu Guochang), previously filed a complaint with the Second Special Court's criminal division, accusing lawyer Qian Zhongdao of embezzlement and breach of trust, and filed an attached civil suit to recover funds. Judge Li Changnian repeatedly opened court to summon the parties, but the matter was adjourned to a later date. Yesterday, the case was heard again. The plaintiff, Wu Guochang, was represented by a lawyer, while the defendant appeared in court with his defense lawyers, Chen Tingrui and Deng Jiabing. According to the defendant's defense lawyer, Chen Tingrui, the case was actually a civil matter of debt. Wang Wenzhi, the manager of Zhengda Bank, previously commissioned the defendant to handle the execution of the Guo Xuanji mortgage debt case, receiving a total of 18,000 yuan. Of this amount, 11,800 yuan was successively delivered to Wang Wenzhi's representative, Zheng Binsen, leaving a balance of 6,200 yuan. After deducting the defendant's legal fees of 2,200 yuan, there was still a shortage of 4,000 yuan. At that time, during the reorganization of Zhengda Bank, a shareholder named Fu Tiezheng wanted to withdraw shares worth 3,000 yuan and contacted the defendant. The defendant discussed this with Wang Wenzhi, who verbally entrusted the defendant to recover the shares and consulted Zheng Baosen, Wu Zhihao, and Hong Yanbin. The defendant proceeded to spend 2,500 yuan to recover Fu's shares, with receipts from Fu and letters from Zheng Wu and others as evidence. Unexpectedly, Wang Wenzhi later denied the stock recovery. At that time, Zheng Shisen and Wu Zhihao had left Shanghai, and Wang urged the defendant to return the remaining 4,000 yuan, entrusting lawyer Zheng Wenkai to handle the matter. After lawyer Zheng's mediation, it was decided that the defendant's procedures for recovering the shares were incomplete, and the defendant was ordered to repay 4,000 yuan, pending Zheng Wu's return to Shanghai to resolve the stock matter. The defendant, respecting the friendship between teacher and student with lawyer Zheng, agreed to sign a contract, awaiting Zheng Wu's return to resolve the matter. The plaintiff then examined the previous accounts and filed a lawsuit. The lawyer stated that he had contacted the plaintiff, stating that the dispute was entirely civil in nature, so why was a criminal lawsuit filed? The plaintiff replied that based on the wishes of the party involved, Wang Wenzhi, the lawsuit was filed to save litigation costs and to expedite the resolution of the case. At noon today, the lawyer agreed with the plaintiff that the defendant would repay 1,500 yuan to settle the matter. The plaintiff has already agreed, he said, and submitted various exhibits to the court. The defendant's statement that he was entrusted by Zhengda Bank to handle the case and the details of recovering the stock were consistent with lawyer Chen's statement. The court questioned the plaintiff's representative lawyer accordingly, who stated that the amount of money and the details mentioned by the defendant were consistent, but that the lawyer did not know about the contact between lawyer Chen and the plaintiff to repay the money and requested a further adjournment to allow both parties to reconcile the civil suit outside the court. The court, after verifying the statements, stated that since the case was a debt dispute and the plaintiff was absent today, the case would be adjourned for another ten days, and a hearing would be held after the plaintiff arrived to make a statement, and then a debate would be opened. The court then adjourned.

Taikoo Company's Ship Sinks Sailboat, Drowning Seven 144

Accident Occurs in the Copper Sand Waters off Wusong; Ningbo Native Association Dispatches Personnel to Negotiate

Datong News Agency reports that the British Taikoo Company's Mlenhof ship collided with a sailboat off the Copper Sand waters outside Wusong on the 26th of last month, causing eight people to fall into the water. Only one person was rescued. Because the incident was not reported to the Maritime Affairs Bureau and the Customs, the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai only began to negotiate with the Taikoo Company yesterday. The details are as follows:

Sinking of Sailboat: Yu Shengcai, a boatman employed by Hu Shengneng's sand and stone company in this port (a Ningbo native), had an elder brother named Yu Shengmao, who owned a sailboat (valued at more than 5,000 yuan), which was used to transport yellow sand and gravel at sea for many years. At about 2:00 AM on the 26th of last month, the sailboat loaded yellow sand and gravel from Shanghai for export. When the ship passed through the Copper Sand waters outside Wusong, it encountered the Taikoo Company's Menhol ship (the ship did not sound its whistle). Because it was late at night, the sailboat was relying on wind power, making it difficult to maneuver. At that time, it was high tide and against the current, so it could not avoid the collision and immediately sank. All eight crew members fell into the water.

Seven Drown: Although the ship knew it had caused the accident and immediately had Western crew members use a longboat to rescue the victims, more than an hour had passed since the sailboat was hit and capsized, so only one crew member, Yu Xiaomao, was rescued. The other seven were nowhere to be found and drowned. Afterwards, although Yu Shengcai, the younger brother of the sailboat owner Yu Shengmao, requested the Yellow Sand and Stone Industry Association to come forward and negotiate with the Taikoo Company, the company only agreed to compensate each deceased person's family with 700 yuan in legal tender. The sailboat side refused to accept because the company would not compensate for the price of the boat and the amount of compensation for the families of the deceased was very small.

Negotiations and Condolences: The Shanghai Yellow Sand and Stone Industry Association, considering that the case involved many lives, did not want to ignore it. Yesterday afternoon, it sent a letter, accompanied by a sailboat owner and the families of the deceased, to the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai to describe the incident. The Association, upon receiving the report, felt that the matter concerned fellow villagers and was very pitiful, so it had dispatched personnel to handle the negotiations with the Taikoo Company with a letter stating the case. The text of the letter from the Native Association to the company is as follows: Our fellow villager Yu Shengmao's sailboat was sunk by the Blue Funnel Line ship (Menhof) on the 26th of last month at about 2:00 AM in the Qian Sha waters. Eight crew members were on board, one was rescued, and the rest were drowned. Yu Shengmao runs a small business and relies on the sailboat for a living. The boat is valued at more than 5,000 yuan. Now, unfortunately, his livelihood has been cut off. The families of the drowned are poor. The dead are gone, and the living have no one to rely on. It is truly pitiful. We have requested our Association to find a way. Therefore, we have sent staff member Zhang Ruihong to respectfully ask your company to have compassion on their misfortune and grant them generous compensation to maintain their livelihoods and comfort the spirits of the deceased. We deeply appreciate your generosity.

Summer Solstice Tomorrow; High Tide in Huangpu River 149

High Tide Begins Tonight at Midnight; Quantity of 11 Feet, 3.5 Inches

Datong News Agency reports that tomorrow is the old lunar calendar's Summer Solstice. According to the prediction of the Shanghai Bund Bureau, there will be a high tide in the Huangpu River at 1:23 AM that day. The magnitude of the tide is expected to be the highest in the Huangpu River in the past six months. The bureau's recorded tidal times and predicted quantities are as follows: The high tide before dawn on the 21st will begin to rise at 11:38 PM tonight. By 0:43 AM tomorrow morning, the tide will accelerate, and the flow rate will reach 1.4 nautical miles per hour. The tide will reach its peak at 1:23 AM tomorrow morning, with a predicted quantity of 11 feet, 3.5 inches. This is less than 1 foot, 7 inches from the 13-foot embankment on the Bund. During this time, low-lying roads may be flooded. The high tide will begin to recede at around 4:00 AM tomorrow morning and will return to normal after 9:00 AM.

Municipal Education Bureau Bans Siming Opera 150

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday issued an order to Xiaoshijie and Fu'an Recreation Ground, stating that Siming Opera, originally named Ningbo Tanhuang, is the most obscene type of opera. It is still banned in its place of origin, Ningbo, and is not allowed to be performed. The Bureau, in consideration of the livelihoods of Siming Opera performers throughout the city, repeatedly ordered them to improve within a limited time. However, after several years, it remains the same. Therefore, in order to maintain public morals, it has been decided to strictly prohibit it across the board, starting with the urban area. In addition to sending separate letters to the Public Security Bureau, the Bureau hereby orders the Recreation Ground to stop performing Siming Opera upon receipt of this order and not to violate it. This order.

Wu Liande Forms Chinese Cremation Association 151

Delivers Speech at Capital Hotel Yesterday Datong News Agency reports that Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the National Maritime Quarantine Service, is extremely enthusiastic about promoting cremation. He has now been hired by the Municipal Government as a member of the Shanghai Cremation Ground Construction Committee. Yesterday afternoon, at the invitation of the Rotary Club, he delivered a speech at the Capital Hotel on the need to promote cremation. The gist of his speech is as follows: Cremation has existed in China since ancient times. Mozi's "On Frugal Burials" advocates cremation. During the Han Dynasty, Buddhism flourished, and cremation became popular. However, Confucianism advocated that the body and hair are received from one's parents and should not be destroyed. As a result, cremation suffered a setback. As a result, one-eleventh of the country's arable land is occupied by graves and tombs. To this day, the country's food supply cannot be self-sufficient and must rely on others. The economic loss is incalculable. To realize Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Principle of People's Livelihood, it is also necessary to promote cremation. In Shanghai alone, there are many coffins and tombs in the suburbs. This is not only unsightly but also unsanitary. Mayor Wu, in view of this, has established the Shanghai Cremation Ground Construction Committee to promote cremation. The committee held its first meeting on the 11th of this month and decided to select public land in front of the Jiangsu Shanghai Municipal Cemetery as the site, covering Nian Mu. The construction cost is tentatively set at 40,000 yuan. In addition to asking the Municipal Government to contribute 30,000 yuan, the remaining 20,000 yuan is to be raised by charitable organizations and enthusiastic individuals in the port. In addition, I am working hard to prepare to organize the Chinese Cremation Association to promote cremation. The association's goals include five items: 1. To promote hygienic, economical, and aesthetic burial methods. 2. To assist the government and the people in using the land currently occupied by graves for agricultural production, so that the government can obtain tax revenue and the people can obtain income. 3. To cooperate with local governments to establish aesthetic cremation grounds to meet the needs of those who wish to be cremated and to suit China's inherent customs and traditions. 4. To work hard to publicize the benefits of cremation. 5. To find ways to contact similar organizations in various countries. In the future, after the association is established, it is hoped that enthusiastic individuals from all walks of life will join the association.

Telephone Council Suggests to Chamber of Commerce: Fight Price Increase 152

Telephone is a Public Utility; Strive for Universality, Otherwise Telephone Rates Will Increase and Users Will Decrease. The Shanghai Special District Telephone Council, considering that the Shanghai Telephone Company is implementing price increases in the current recession, which has caused social unrest, has suggested to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which is holding its general membership meeting today, that it present the price increase issue for discussion and adopt the proposed resolution. The original text is as follows: Sirs, since the Shanghai Telephone Company, in the current recession, presumptuously hopes to satisfy its desire for an annual interest rate of 1%, it has illegally raised prices, causing social unrest. Considering that telephone is a public utility and a tool for communication, we should strive for universality and adopt the principle of low price and high volume. Even if the company is concerned with its business, it should profit from volume. Otherwise, telephone rates will increase, and the number of users will decrease. As a result, commerce will be restricted, and the company will fail. Since the implementation of the new price increase regulations, the company's telephone directory for the winter of the year before last contained 488 pages, while the telephone directory for the spring of this year contained only 426 pages. With 76 households per page, the number of users who have removed their telephones this year due to being unable to afford the increase is 4,500. This figure does not include those who removed their telephones after the directory was printed. The company's statement that several thousand users have automatically requested installation after the implementation of the new regulations is simply deception. This fact proves that the Council's statement that the more the telephone rates increase, the fewer the number of users, is true. Furthermore, according to reports from users in various districts, the meter readings are inaccurate, with the number of calls being recorded more than a hundred times. This extra sacrifice will affect the company's reputation. Your Chamber is the commercial center of the city, and the increase in telephone rates is of direct interest to all members. The Council has conducted a thorough study of the issue and has proposed the following measures for the general meeting to discuss and adopt to facilitate resolution: 1. Whether for basic calls or excess calls, charge 2 cents per call. However, in consideration of the company's business, commercial telephones must have a minimum monthly basic charge of 10 yuan, and residential telephones must have a minimum monthly basic charge of 6.5 yuan. 2. The call charges between the Special District and the city should be eliminated. 3. For the sake of credibility, each telephone should be equipped with a meter. 4. Once the company's income exceeds the annual interest rate of 1%, the Board of Directors of the Bureau of Public Works should convene a meeting to discuss a reduction in rates. 5. The above measures should be implemented for a trial period of one year. If the company does not accept these measures, then the various trade associations should instruct their members to stop paying their bills and allow their telephones to be removed. In addition, a request should be submitted to the central government to issue public bonds and take over the telephone company. If we proceed in this manner, it will be easier to resolve the issue. Furthermore, the implementation of the above improvement measures will inevitably attract more users. This is necessary for the company to ensure its development. Therefore, we respectfully submit our views to your Chamber for consideration and adoption for the benefit of all users in the city.

In order to promote the travel interest of Chinese people, China Travel Service has launched the organization of the Snow Leopard Mountain Tour Group, which is scheduled to depart from Shanghai at 5:00 PM on June 30 and return to Shanghai at 5:00 AM on July 4. The number of participants is 20, the cost is 20 yuan for group members and 22 yuan for non-group members. The itinerary is as follows: Depart from Shanghai by the New Jiangtian Wheel at 5:00 PM on June 30, arrive in Ningbo at 5:00 AM on July 1, have breakfast on the wheel, leave the wheel at 8:00 AM and take a rickshaw to the bus station, take a specially prepared bus at 7:00 AM, arrive at the mountain entrance pavilion at about 9:00 AM, change to a mountain sedan to go up the mountain, rest at the company's guest house, and have lunch. After lunch, walk or take a mountain sedan to visit Qianzhangyan, Miaogaotai, Feixueting, Liuzhi Bridge, etc. On July 2, walk or take a mountain sedan to visit the upper, middle and lower hidden pools (lunch at the upper hidden pool). On July 3, take a sedan to Tingxia at 7:00 AM, then take a bamboo raft to Xikou (this section is the most interesting) to visit Wenchang Pavilion, Wuling Elementary School, Jiang's Ancestral Hall, etc. At 10:00 AM, take a special car from Xikou, arrive in Ningbo for lunch at about 12:00 AM, have free time to visit after lunch, and take the New Jiangtian Wheel away from Ningbo at 4:00 PM. Return to Shanghai at 5:00 AM on July 4.

Pindou Sentenced to Ten Months Imprisonment 164

Mr. Pindou, the manager of the Italian Bank, was sentenced to 14 months imprisonment and fined 2,000 lire last week by the Italian Consulate Court for being accused of faking a theft in an attempt to defraud the insurance company of compensation. For extortion of usurious loans, the court interrogated the victim on Thursday of last week, and the hearing was postponed to Thursday of this week to allow the defendant's account books to be examined. At the time of the hearing, the hearing officers summoned witnesses and examined the account books, proving that the defendant was guilty of extortion of usury, and sentenced him to ten months imprisonment and fined him 3,000 lire. The defendant has declared an appeal in both cases, but the appeal will have to be heard in Rhodes Island in the Mediterranean in the future.

Apprentice Chen Amao Donates to the Chinese Epidemic Hospital Chen Amao, an apprentice from Sheng Sheng Iron Factory, is from Shaanxi and is 13 years old. He comes from a normal family and works hard. He passed the intersection of Huade Road, Tilanqiao the other day and read about the Chinese Epidemic Hospital, which is saving epidemic patients, giving treatment and medicine, and not charging any money. He was moved and generously donated three yuan, his two months' worth of monthly wages. The hospital staff wanted to ask his name, but he didn't say anything and left. Everyone was very surprised. So they hid and followed him, and finally learned the truth. As a result, all the colleagues in the hospital are working harder. This proves that the apprentice is enthusiastic about charity and is admirable, so I write it in detail.

Various Local Organizations Periodically Hold Farewell for World Games Representatives 175

At the YMCA on Eight Immortals Bridge on the 24th

Fourteen organizations including the Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, General Labor Union, Municipal Farmers' Association, Chinese Culture Construction Association, University Faculty Union, China Insurance Company, and Jingwu Athletic Association of this city held a preparatory meeting in the Municipal Government conference room at 2:00 PM on the 18th to bid farewell to the Chinese delegation participating in the World Games. Those present were Zhou Xuexiang (Municipal General Labor Union), Jiang Jianbai (Municipal Education Bureau, Municipal Sports Association, Chinese Culture Construction Association, University Faculty Union), Qian Ruiting (Garrison Headquarters), Wei Langxuan (Jingwu Athletic Association), Yang Guozhu (China Aviation Association), Luo Beichen and Chen Dahe (China Insurance Company), Yu Zhenhui (Municipal Farmers' Association), Li Jianyuan (Stadium), Sun Yong (Social Affairs Bureau), Li Dachao (Municipal Government), and Huang Zhaoxiong (Municipal Party Headquarters). Chairman Li Dachao made the following report: (A) Report Items: The Chairman reported, "We have gathered everyone here today to discuss the matter of bidding farewell to the delegation participating in the World Games. We would like to, before the delegation departs, set a date to gather people from all walks of life in the city to hold a grand farewell party to express our comfort and encouragement. As for the date and location of the event, as well as all the preparatory matters that should be carried out, please express your opinions and discuss them together to make a decision." Chen Tianhe, representative of China Insurance Company, reported on the significance of the company jointly gathering various organizations to bid farewell to the athletes attending the World Games and the progress of preparations, for reference. (B) Discussion Items: Regarding the case of how the name of the farewell party should be decided, it was decided that the name would be "Shanghai Municipal All Circles Farewell Conference for the Delegation Attending the World Games." Regarding the case of how the general affairs, arrangement, reception, and all other preparatory matters that should be carried out at the conference should be distributed and handled, it was resolved to publicly recommend the Municipal Government, Municipal Party Headquarters, Municipal Education Bureau, Municipal Sports Association, Municipal General Labor Union, and China Insurance Company to organize, with the Municipal Government in charge. Regarding the case of selecting the location of the conference, it was resolved to borrow the YMCA on Eight Immortals Bridge. Regarding the case of the date of the conference, it was decided to hold it at 4:00 PM on June 24th. Regarding the case of selecting the presidium of the conference, it was resolved to invite Mayor Wu, Commander Yang, Director Pan, Tong Xingbai, and Song Hanzhang to serve. Regarding the case of soliciting various municipal organizations to participate in the conference, it was resolved to notify them by letter and announce it in the newspaper. Regarding the case of how the expenses for the conference should be determined and allocated, it was resolved that the expenses for the conference would be estimated at 200 yuan, and each participating organization should pay 5 yuan. If it is insufficient, please request assistance from the Municipal Government. Regarding the case of how to bid farewell to the delegation when they leave Shanghai by ship, it was resolved: 1. Send two flower baskets to the ship in the name of the conference; 2. Representatives of all organizations participating in the conference must all go to the pier to see them off; 3. Request the Public Security Bureau to send a military band to play music at the pier to bid farewell; 4. Request the Aviation Association to send two airplanes to accompany the ship until it reaches Wusongkou.

School Investigation: An Overview of the Shanghai Jewish School (Part 1) 191

— Hu Zuyin

The Shanghai Jewish School is located at 544 Seymour Road in the Western District of the Public Concession. The school is large in scale and well-equipped. This article is based on materials provided by Ms. Solomon, the principal of the school, and we are very grateful for her donation of a booklet outlining the school's general situation.

I. The Largest Jewish School in the Far East

The Shanghai Jewish School was founded in 1902 with the purpose of providing Jewish children with a sound education that would enable them to adapt to the struggles of life, become self-respecting young men and women, and good citizens. The school initially held classes in a bungalow in Hongkou, with fewer than ten students enrolled at that time. The curriculum consisted only of English and Hebrew. Later, the school gradually developed and expanded, and by 1930, the total number of students had increased to about one hundred. However, the school buildings were small and the facilities were simple, while the number of students was very large, so the Municipal Council considered it quite dangerous and often hoped that the school would relocate.

At this time, an Englishman named Isaac S. Perry passed away. In his will, Perry designated a donation of 150,000 taels of silver for the construction of a new school building for the Jewish school, provided that the Jewish people in Shanghai raise an equal amount of funds to serve as a school maintenance fund. Soon, the school maintenance fund was raised by the Jewish people, and a plot of land at 544 Seymour Road, next to the Jewish synagogue, was purchased to begin construction of the new school building. The new school building was completed in 1931, and all students then moved into the new school building to attend classes.

The new school building was designed and supervised by the Jewish engineer C. H. Gonda. The entire school building can be said to represent the most modern school in the Far East. All sanitary and hygiene facilities are modern. The corridors and classrooms on all levels are spacious, bright, and well-ventilated. According to the principal, many public and private schools often send people to visit the school when constructing their own school buildings, in order to learn from it. The entire school building can accommodate 300 students and is the largest Jewish school in the Far East. The school currently has three departments: middle school, elementary school, and kindergarten, and accepts both male and female students. There are approximately 250 students in total. Many Jewish children residing in North China or abroad also wish to attend the school.

II. School Buildings and Facilities

The school building is 口-shaped and has two floors. The entire building is constructed with steel and cement and is quite sturdy. The school building is surrounded by gates or side doors leading to the outside, making it very convenient for students to enter and exit. On the lower floor of the school building, near the west entrance, are the principal's office and the infirmary. To the left is the auditorium, and opposite the main entrance are the student dining hall and kitchen. To the right are the kindergarten, lower grade classrooms, and elementary school toilets. Sand filtration water pipes are installed along both sides of the corridor. Upstairs are the upper grade and middle school classrooms, art room, library, girls' sewing room, classroom office, storage room, etc. There is no student laboratory or science room, which is a slight imperfection. The music room is combined with the auditorium for joint use. The sports field is 150 feet long and 85 feet wide and has two basketball courts, two playgrounds, one handball court, and two large sandboxes. Students can also use the open space next to the synagogue.

The facilities in each classroom are quite perfect. There are a total of nine ordinary classrooms: each elementary school classroom can accommodate 45 students, and each middle school classroom can accommodate 25 students. Each classroom is connected to the corridor and is mostly south-facing. The light enters from the left side. Blackboards are installed on the side of the classroom where the light is concentrated. All classrooms use steel windows that can be opened in three places. There are two vertical window doors in the middle and one horizontal transom window at the top and bottom. Therefore, windows can be opened for ventilation even in the severe winter weather without causing students to catch a cold. The curtains are either automatic roller blinds or beaded curtains.

Yarn and Cotton: Manufacturers Heavily Selling Short; Cotton Yarn Rises and Falls in Distant Months 195

The yarn and cloth market changed several times a day, and the situation became more chaotic. The price of raw cotton trended upwards, and there were rumors of a short squeeze, causing fluctuations in cotton yarn. However, the current yarn business did not show any healthy momentum, and the yarn stockpiled in the yarn and cloth warehouses still had no ability to move. Therefore, those who went long had little interest. The second session opened in the afternoon with a crazy jump, followed by a massive short sale by a certain factory, and a certain company vigorously throwing out. The closing price suddenly fell.

Spot Yarn Uniquely Rises in the Current Month

In the morning opening of the spot yarn market, overseas yarn and cotton conditions were slightly down, and all months saw a return to flat, falling by 0.03, 0.04, 0.05, and 0.06 yuan. The second and third sessions were still normal. By the third closing session, due to the crazy jump in raw cotton, market sentiment was excited, causing the related yarn market to rise in response.
