Cornerstone Laying Special Edition of Qiujiang Wharf

Introduction 208

— Kong Xiangxi

The Shanghai Qiujiang Wharf will hold a cornerstone laying ceremony on June 20 and publish a special edition. Those in charge asked me to write an introduction. I think the origin of the Qiujiang Wharf and the process of years of preparation have been described in detail by those who are in charge, and there is no need for my wise words. However, at the beginning of this cornerstone laying, I would like to express my feelings to the people of the country. Since our country opened up to trade, ships have gathered, and various shipping companies have set up wharves on both sides of the Huangpu River as places for ships to berth, which has been the case for decades. However, due to the narrowness and shallowness of the river, it is very inconvenient to load and unload goods. The construction of the Qiujiang Wharf will greatly facilitate the transportation and storage of goods, and it will not be difficult to develop our overseas commerce. This is of great importance to the future of our country's international trade. This is the first thing that makes me happy. Shanghai's prosperity is concentrated in the concession area, and the urban area is declining day by day. Since the establishment of the municipal government and the implementation of the plan to prosper Greater Shanghai, the development of industry and commerce is the first priority. The establishment of the wharf will greatly contribute to the development of industry and commerce and will greatly benefit the prosperity of Greater Shanghai. This is the second thing that makes me happy. Transportation construction is the most important facility of the government in recent years, because it has a close relationship with other industries. In recent years, the government has established the Central Trust Bureau, and the Ministry of Industry has established various factories and markets. However, these cannot prosper without transportation. The establishment of the wharf is entrusted to the general industry and commerce. Therefore, the establishment of the wharf will greatly assist state-owned enterprises. This is the third thing that makes me happy. The hard work of those in charge for several years of preparation and the support of all parties to promote the success of this event are also what I am happy and grateful for. Today, on the day of the cornerstone laying, I have expressed my feelings as above. Gentlemen of the country, please give your advice!

Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi 209

The Relationship between Building Qiujiang Wharf and Prospering the Shanghai Urban Area 210

— Wu Tiecheng

In the past, before the rise of railways and ships, the characteristic of all prosperous commercial places was "masts standing like forests," which shows that water transportation has long been related to the development of cities. Since the advent of railways, there have been tools on land that can carry heavy loads over long distances. Therefore, remote hinterlands have also become major towns due to factors such as terrain and products. For example, Berlin in Germany is not along the coast, nor is it traversed by giant rivers. It has become one of the world's largest cities solely because of its railway hub. However, waterway transportation is inferior to railways in terms of speed, but it has an advantage in terms of economy. Therefore, even in areas with crisscrossing railway tracks, waterway transportation cannot be abandoned. For example, of the 25 million tons of goods imported into Berlin each year, no less than 10 million tons come via canals. As for the actual sea points where ocean transportation gathers, namely the locations of so-called sea ports, waterway transportation is the lifeline for the development of industry and commerce. Its importance is greater than the railway transportation connecting the hinterland.

Shanghai is located at the mouth of our country's largest navigable river and is very close to the ocean. Its natural condition is suitable for forming a deep-water port. The 1.94 million square kilometers of land in the Yangtze River basin has a natural barrier and almost entirely uses it as a port for loading and unloading goods. In addition, most of the commerce in southern China passes through Shanghai due to the natural limitations of the hinterland and draft of the coastal commercial ports between Hong Kong and Shanghai. Also, due to the terrain, there are no deep-water ports in northern China that can be used, so all commerce is centered on Shanghai. Therefore, Shanghai's position in ocean transportation can be said to be particularly superior.

In terms of inland river transportation, the waterway from Shanghai up the Yangtze River to Hankou is excellent. Ships with a draft of about 3 meters can pass in winter, and ships with a draft of about 9 meters can pass in summer. From Hankou upwards, special ships can be used to navigate 1,300 kilometers in summer. Most of the other larger tributaries are suitable for the navigation of sand boats and small ships. The import and export goods of the commercial ports near each tributary are concentrated in Shanghai. Therefore, Shanghai's position in inland river transportation can also be said to be particularly superior.

From the above, the development of Shanghai from a small county town into a metropolis with a population of 3.5 million, the largest commercial port in our country, and one of the ten largest commercial ports in the world, is it accidental? However, if there had been no dredging of the Huangpu River and the equipment of wharves and ships, the benefits of water transportation would not have been obvious, and it would not have been possible to leap from a scattered fishing village to today's prosperous urban area in a few decades. From this, it can be seen that the prosperity of a place's industry and commerce depends not only on natural conditions and geographical advantages but also on human construction.

Shanghai's existing wharf facilities are the foundation of its previous prosperity, but compared with modern European and American seaports, they are still inferior in many ways. In particular, the lack of connection between water and land transportation makes it a major shortcoming, even though goods are concentrated from the interior or distributed to the interior via the Shanghai Railway, which is efficient and economical. Secondly, the total length of deep-water wharves with a depth of more than 9 meters (30 feet) below the lowest tide level is only about 3,100 meters, including both sides of the Huangpu River. Let's look at the Port of Hamburg, one of the major ports in Europe, where the length of wharves for seagoing vessels is no less than 35,000 meters. From this, it can be seen that the length of Shanghai's existing wharves is not enough to meet the needs of development. In recent decades, Shanghai's wharf facilities have not been significantly improved. If we remain complacent today, then in the long run, it will be as the report of the Shanghai Port Technical Advisory Committee in the tenth year of the Republic of China stated: "If the improvement project is not implemented, ships with deeper drafts will inevitably be attracted by foreign distribution centers, and Shanghai will be reduced to a second-class commercial port. Not only will the interests of this port be greatly damaged, but its impact will also affect the entire country!"

Therefore, in order to maintain and enhance Shanghai's prosperity, new construction related to water transportation, namely the expansion and improvement of wharf facilities, cannot be delayed. There have been plans to open the Wusong Commercial Port. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be realized in a short period of time. Therefore, the Central Bank has invested in the construction of the Qiujiang Wharf. After its completion in the future, the length of Shanghai's deep-water wharves can be increased by 1,400 meters. Even in the first phase of the project, it can be increased by 880 meters. The connection with roads and railways and the facilities for warehouses and freight yards have also been carefully planned. The improvement of the economic conditions of transportation between Shanghai and various places at home and abroad will be self-evident. The reduction of transportation costs is enough to promote the development of industry and commerce, and it can also indirectly increase the prosperity of the urban area. The distance between the city center and Qiujiang Wharf is far away, and it is the closest hinterland. Its serious development can be expected!

Mayor of Shanghai Wu Tiecheng 211

Construction Plan of Qiujiang Wharf 212

— Song Ziliang

In the spring of the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, in order to develop international trade, support state-owned enterprises, and promote the prosperity of the Shanghai urban area, the Central Bank decided to build Qiujiang Wharf and warehouses to facilitate transportation. The wharf business is large in scale and the project is complicated. It is difficult to achieve effective assistance without gathering specialized talents to study together. Minister Kong had seen this, so on the fourth day of the month, he was ordered to form the Qiujiang Wharf Design Committee with Mr. Chen Jian'an, Ye Zhuotang, Mr. Cha Tingzhi (CHATLEY), Mr. Liu Hongsheng, and Ziliang. In May of the twenty-fourth year, Mr. Zhang Gongkuang and Mr. Xu Keting were appointed as members. In August of the same year, after the design work was completed, he was ordered to reorganize the Design Committee into a Construction Committee, with the same members. With the elegant intentions of the members, he was elected as the chairman of the committee.

Looking back since receiving the order, it will be two years in an instant. The responsibility is heavy and the talent is shallow, and there is always the fear of falling. Fortunately, Minister Kong's guidance and the assistance of the members are always obtained. Although there is no special achievement in the wharf work, on the occasion of its scale, the motives for construction, the outline of the plan, and the contents of the first phase of the wharf project, etc., are briefly described below:

Chairman of the Qiujiang Wharf Construction Committee Song Ziliang 213

(1) Motives for Building the Wharf

The Huangpu shore near the Qiujiang estuary in the Yinhang District of Shanghai has long been regarded by the navigation industry and the League of Nations investigation team as an ideal wharf area, suitable for the construction of docks and wharves. Its shoreline is long and straight, the river water is deep and wide, and the ships are safer and more convenient to travel and berth than other areas of the Huangpu River. In particular, it is close to the commercial and industrial center of Greater Shanghai, which will have a great relationship with the development of international trade and the transit of import and export goods in the future. Ships now berth here, and when importing and exporting, they pass the Shentan outside the Wusong Estuary without having to wait for the tide to rise and fall, and can sail freely. It is found that the rented areas along the Huangpu River are narrow, the water volume is low, and various large and small ships gather in them, which is very crowded. The shipping routes of heavy mail ships are too narrow, which makes it inconvenient to travel in them, and it is easy to encounter unexpected events if you are not careful. If there is a wharf at the Qiujiang estuary where ships can berth, this dangerous and time-consuming voyage can be avoided, which is convenient for cargo transportation and saves costs. This is because of the superior natural conditions that are suitable for the construction of the wharf.

Moreover, the wharf business has a great impact on the prosperity of the market. All industries such as transportation, transportation, finance, insurance, etc. can rely on it to flourish. Once the wharf is established, the prosperity of the city center can be expected in the near future. For this reason, we resolutely decided to build this wharf.

Member of the Qiujiang Wharf Construction Committee Zhang Gongquan 214

(2) Outline of the Wharf Construction Plan

The above-mentioned land is located at Huangpu No. 90, Shangzi, north of the Qiujiang estuary, about 800 mu of beach land, and about 300 mu of land in the Zhou Yi San Liang maps. It has been purchased and filled to 19 feet above the Wusong estuary level, and can be used to build a wharf and warehouses with a length of about 3,000 feet and a width of about 1,000 feet. Such a large area must be based on predicting the future number of industries and on the principle of not damaging the interests of investment. The system for planning and proceeding is to select the important plots among them and build them in stages, so as to conform to the principles of economy and achieve the purpose of investment.

The entire wharf plan is divided into three phases. In the first phase, two wharves will be built first, each with a length of 590 feet, which can accommodate the largest mail ships, such as the Empress of the Changxing Shipping Company and the President of the Da Lai Shipping Company. Two two-story steel-framed concrete warehouses and two iron-roofed flat warehouses are required. The steel-framed warehouses can be increased to four stories at any time, and the iron-roofed flat warehouses can be demolished, and the site can be used to build steel-framed warehouses, as well as offices, staff dormitories, etc. The construction cost is about 5 million yuan. The location is in the south section of the wharf area, accounting for about one-third of the area. It has been contracted and is expected to be completed by the end of October this year, and can be put into operation. If necessary, the second phase of the project is planned to be continued.

When the entire plan is completed, there will be a straight shoreline of about 3,000 feet, eight four-story steel-framed warehouses, and iron-roofed warehouses. At the south end, there is a separate horse-drawn boat port. Although there are about 1,000 feet of warehouses behind, the Shanghai municipal road Xu Daopuxi Road runs north and south from the city center to the middle and far green of the wharf, and Wuquan Road runs horizontally in between. In the northern part of the wharf area, there is a public wharf of about 350 feet long. All the wharf decks in front of each warehouse are equipped with mechanical equipment for transporting goods, such as cranes and railway tracks. In the wharf area, along both sides of Puxi Road, there is space reserved for the construction of travel agencies, shipping companies, transportation companies, automobile companies, hotels, and other agencies related to the wharf.

Shanghai is not only the largest commercial port in the Far East, but also one of the top ten commercial ports in the world. Its supply of goods is larger than any other commercial port in Asia. By water, it controls the throat of the Yangtze River. By land, the railway runs across it and can be connected with major domestic trunk lines. All imported goods must be distributed from Shanghai to the Yangtze River basin, such as Nanjing, Pukou, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, and then to Hankou, and then from the Yangtze River basin, they are transported to the interior. The goods from the interior and the various ports of the Yangtze River must also be concentrated in Shanghai for transportation and export. Therefore, Shanghai is the general hub for the distribution of import and export goods from the provinces along the Yangtze River. The Qiujiang Wharf plans to lay railway tracks in front and behind the warehouses to connect to the Songhu Line, so that it can be jointly transported with the various lines that have opened to traffic in Shanghai, such as the Beijing-Zhejiang, Pingjin, and Yuehan lines. All goods arriving in Shanghai from overseas can be unloaded and transported to the interior by train as soon as the ship arrives, and the export goods from the interior can also be loaded from the train to the Qiujiang Wharf and unloaded onto the ship for direct transport overseas. Regardless of import or export goods, there is no need to fall into the warehouse, which saves time and reduces costs. There are three railway tracks behind the warehouses and one in front of the wharf, which merge into one at the intersection of Wuquan Road and connect to the Songhu Line along the Huangpu River in the northern part of the city center, about 9 kilometers long. According to the estimate of the Lianglu Administration, the construction cost is about 750,000 yuan in national currency. How to raise and bear the construction cost, how to design the various projects, is now being discussed and handled with the bureau. After it is built in the future, it can achieve the effect of water-land combined transportation. There are also thousands of acres of vacant land near the wharf. In the Greater Shanghai plan, it is planned to be used as an airport, and at the same time, a place is designated on the river surface for seaplanes to berth. If these two become a reality in the future, the transportation of goods at the wharf will not only be connected by water and land, but will also be connected by water, land, and air. This is the unique feature of Qiujiang Wharf, which is not only unmatched by other wharves in the Far East, but will also become one of the best wharves in the world.

Perspective View of Qiujiang Wharf 215

Regarding the water supply equipment for ships, the fire protection work of the wharf and warehouses, and the public security and cleaning issues, the existing equipment of the various wharves in this port is not perfect, especially the convenience for travelers and those who pick them up has not been paid attention to. Qiujiang Wharf is different, with careful consideration and perfect equipment everywhere. The paths for passengers to travel back and forth are separated from the path for transporting goods, and the two do not interfere with each other. There is a reception room for passengers and those who pick them up to rest. There is also a store that sells food and drinks, as well as famous Chinese products, for passengers to purchase. In addition, there are lookout stations, customs baggage and passport inspection offices, parking spaces, police stations, and information desks. In short, passengers are given every convenience to stay or travel back and forth.

(3) Contents of the First Phase of the Project

Appropriately along the Huangpu River to the north of the Qiujiang estuary, about 1,500 feet long, a large straight-line wharf is built here. Because a barge port of 220 feet long is temporarily set up in the middle section, the shoreline is recessed inward, so the wharf is formed into two seats. Along the barge port, that is, in the middle of the two wharves, there is a two-story office building. The upper floor is the wharf office, and the lower floor is the customs inspection office and passenger reception room. On both sides of the office building, north and south, there are two two-story steel-framed warehouses. In addition, at the north and south ends, there are two warehouses that are almost identical. The back part to the west is a flat cargo stacking field, surrounded by roads. The residential dormitories are located in the southwest corner of the entire area. The various projects designed are described in detail below:

(A) Wharf

The wharf is divided into two seats, each with a length of 590 feet. The lower part is filled with wooden bridges, and the upper part is made of steel-framed concrete. The wooden bridge is driven below the average water level to prevent it from rotting easily. The wharf deck is 50 feet wide and has all the mooring equipment. Below, there are mooring gears spaced 50 feet apart, and there are crossbeams for mooring barges. There are rotary cranes on the deck, and a low-level deck is built below so that small boats and barges can still work normally when the tide is low.

Member of the Qiujiang Wharf Construction Committee Chen Xing 216

(B) Warehouse

(1) Steel-framed Warehouse

The two steel-framed warehouses are fixed buildings. The lower part is built with 100-foot and 90-foot long wooden floors, and the upper part is made of steel-framed concrete. The foundation is prepared for four-story buildings. However, only two stories are built at present, and the remaining two stories are planned to be added when the business expands in the future. In this way, not only is the opening cost saved, but also when the building is raised, the foundation will not be re-driven, which will hinder the use of the original two-story warehouse. Each warehouse is 220 feet long and 130 feet wide. The upper floor is for long-term storage of goods, while the lower floor is for short-term storage of goods.

(2) Iron-roofed Flat Warehouse

The two iron-roofed flat warehouses are temporary buildings for short-term storage of goods. Each is 220 feet long and 80 feet wide, with three bridges leading directly to the wharf deck. If a fixed steel-framed warehouse is built, the iron-roofed flat warehouse can be demolished and moved to the rear for use, and the site will be used to build the steel-framed warehouse. Because the scope of business is not yet known, it is chosen for its low price and easy movement. There is no great loss in demolishing and reinstalling it. If a mail ship over 5-600 feet long is berthed at the wharf, the rotary crane on the wharf deck can lift the cargo from the ship's fore cabin to the front of the iron-roofed shed; the cargo from the aft cabin can be lifted to any receiving platform of the steel-framed warehouse, and then the goods can be stored separately according to their long-term and short-term storage properties. Not only is the procedure quick, but it also saves transportation costs.

Member of the Qujiang Wharf Construction Committee, Xu Kan 217

(3) Warehouse capacity and internal/external cargo handling equipment.

Member of the Qujiang Wharf Construction Committee, Ye Zhuotang 218

The total existing warehouse capacity is approximately 15,000 tons. Outside the warehouse, on the dock deck, there are rail-mounted cranes, which can directly lift goods from the ship's hold to any floor of the steel-framed warehouse without the need for manual handling. In front of the warehouse, at the cargo inspection area, there is a duplex straight-line crane that can directly lift goods from the lower level of the warehouse to the upper level. All cranes include four crane trucks, two inclined rollers, and one 1-ton and one 6-ton mobile elevator vehicle each, and one hundred and fifty cargo-rolling pulleys. If necessary, several 1-ton and 10.5-ton semi-rotary cranes will be added. The rear part of the warehouse is equipped with an elevator. Therefore, a one-way traffic pattern can be maintained inside the warehouse.

(C) Office.

The office is located in the middle of the warehouse, two stories high, 220 feet long, and built of reinforced concrete bricks and tiles. The upper floor is the wharf office, and the lower floor is arranged as a customs inspection office and passenger reception room in accordance with the new customs regulations. It is built in the center of the wharf along the bank, making it the administrative center of the wharf's traffic management, which seems more convenient for business.

(D) Staff Residences.

The staff residences are built at the southwest end of the wharf area, equidistant and not far from the wharf warehouses. The project includes one residence for the wharf manager, two residences for the wharf supervisors, two residences for the customs inspectors, one dormitory for staff that can accommodate forty people, and six two-bay two-story houses, and twelve one-bay two-story houses.

(E) Cargo Storage Yards and Roads.

Behind the warehouses, etc., is a cargo storage yard with an area of approximately 257,400 square feet, divided into nine rectangular areas. Each area is surrounded by roads, temporarily for the accumulation of heavy goods that are not affected by the weather. In the future, it will be used as the base for building warehouses. The roads are paved with a solid coal layer.

(F) Traffic Routes.

In the public road system of the urban area, two major trunk lines are designated. One is a north-south line, which is Puxi Road, starting from Yangshupu, along the west bank of the Huangpu River, passing about 1,000 feet behind the wharf, that is, parallel to the north and south in the middle of the wharf line and Jungong Road, to Wusong. One is an east-west line, which is Puxi Road, starting from Yangshupu, along the west bank of the Huangpu River, passing about 1,000 feet behind the wharf, that is, parallel to the north in the middle of the wharf line and Jungong Road, to Wusong. One is an east-west line, which is Wuquan Road, starting from the north end bank of the first phase of the wharf use area, crossing Jungong Road and reaching the center of the urban area. Other roads parallel to Wuquan Road in the east-west direction include Xiangyin Road, Hairong Road, and Haitang Road. Except for the section of Wuquan Road from the city center area to Jungong Road, which has been built long ago, and the current construction of Jungong Road to the wharf area; the rest have not yet been built. However, the section of Puxi Road in the wharf area will be built simultaneously with the completion of the first phase of the wharf project. The road surfaces of each route are planned to be paved with asphalt and are wide in area. Among them, Wuquan Road and Puxi Road are particularly so.

Member of the Qujiang Wharf Construction Committee, Chadley 219

The area from the rear of the wharf to Puxi Road, in the first phase of the project, has already been provided with a cinder road network, that is, the roads around the cargo storage yard mentioned above, one of which is larger and directly connects to the north gate, and is connected to Wuquan Road. Therefore, Wuquan Road is the main road for land transportation at the wharf. The completion of this road can coincide with the completion of the first phase of the wharf project.

When the wharf starts operating, there will be three traffic routes in the wharf area: (1) From Wuquan Road, turn into Jungong Road to reach Yangshupu Road; (2) From Wuquan Road, pass through the city center area and turn into Qimei Road to reach Dihisiwei Road; (3) From Wuquan Road, pass through the city center area and turn into Jiangwan Road to reach North Sichuan Road. The driving time on these three routes is less than twenty minutes, which can be said to be extremely convenient.

Member of the Qujiang Wharf Construction Committee, Liu Hongsheng 220

The above is a general outline of the plan to build the wharf. The entire project can be completed in the autumn. The only feature of the wharf is that it is planned to lay railway tracks to connect to the Songhu Line, and that vacant land near the wharf can be used to build an airport. If these things become reality in the future, then combined water, land, and air transportation will be available. Passenger transportation, cargo, and mail transportation will save time and expenses, international trade will be promoted as a result, and both national economy and people's livelihood will benefit. In that case, the Qujiang Wharf will not only be able to take the lead among the docks in the east, but will also be able to compete with the world's major docks without being inferior. This is what we can expect.

What's more, all shipping facilities upstream and downstream of the Huangpu River are deeply related to the development of our country's industry and commerce. They must be managed independently by the Chinese people in a thorough manner, so that they can be improved day by day and strive for development; the construction of Qujiang Wharf is indeed its beginning.

The Position of Qujiang Wharf in China's International Trade 221

— Guo Chengwen

The wharf industry is closely related to international trade. With excellent wharf facilities, cargo handling is convenient, which not only saves time but also reduces costs. As a result, large-scale trade is attracted. Now, all commercially developed countries in the world are building complete wharves in their commercial ports to facilitate the loading and unloading of import and export goods.

Shanghai is China's trade center. More than 50% of the country's import and export trade is concentrated in Shanghai, and about 40% of the domestic entrepot trade is also monopolized by Shanghai. From this, it can be seen that Shanghai is the largest port for domestic and foreign trade in China. As trade is prosperous, the wharf industry is also quite developed. According to the Shanghai Port Guide (1934), the total length of the beaches on both sides of the Huangpu River in Pudong and Puxi is 253.475 English feet, of which 38.770 English feet are used as ordinary cargo wharves, 27.440 English feet are used as special cargo wharves, 13.025 English feet are used as shipyards, 19.255 English feet are used as roads and public or customs wharves, 27.480 English feet are used as industrial beaches, and 5.535 English feet are used as creeks. The remaining 121.970 English feet are undeveloped beaches. There are more than 100 major wharves and shipyards in total. Although Shanghai's wharves are more developed than other ports in China, their nature is not yet sound and their equipment is not complete. It is inevitable that they will be stretched to cope with current needs, let alone promote the development of future trade. In terms of nature, the biggest shortcomings of Shanghai's current wharves are that there are too few wharves operated by the Chinese, and the wharf industry is almost entirely in the hands of foreigners. According to a survey of the wharves on both sides of the Huangpu River in Pudong and Puxi (including shipyards), there are about 92 in total, of which 15 belong to the Chinese government, and 19 belong to private Chinese merchants, totaling 34, accounting for more than one-third of the total number of wharves in Shanghai. The remaining two-thirds are owned by the United Kingdom, Japan, the United States, and France. Moreover, the wharves operated by China, except for those operated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the San Bei Company, are mostly small wharves with simple equipment, or are only used for loading and unloading coal. Their scale is not as powerful as those operated by foreigners. As a result, the loading and unloading of goods is inevitably controlled by foreigners. Secondly, there are too few public wharves, and most of them are private. Among the 92 wharves in Shanghai, only 15 are operated by the Chinese government (including the wharves operated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the railway wharves, and the municipal government wharves), and only 2 belong to the Public Concession's Public Works Department, totaling 17, accounting for only 18% of the total number of wharves. From this, it can be seen that most of Shanghai's wharves are privately owned. The excessive number of such private wharves not only makes it difficult to achieve uniform loading and unloading fees and procedures, but also often results in high costs, which directly affect the transportation costs of goods and indirectly affect the development of trade.

Attached: Classification of Nationality of Important Wharves on the East and West Banks of the Huangpu River

Secondly, in terms of equipment, Shanghai's wharves have not been able to fully facilitate the loading and unloading of goods. Shanghai's existing wharves cannot accommodate the berthing of first-class ocean-going ships. According to the Shanghai Port Guide, the length of Shanghai's wharves that can accommodate ships with a draft of 28 feet is about 10,000 English feet, and the length of those that can accommodate ships with a draft of 30 feet is only 6,000 English feet. However, the commerce of the Pacific Ocean will inevitably be carried by ships with deeper drafts in the future. The draft of large ships should reach 33 feet. It is clear that Shanghai's wharves are insufficient to meet the needs of large ships for berthing and unloading. As for the various equipment on the wharves, they are even more simple. The most important equipment for a wharf is cranes, light railways, barges, and warehouses. Among Shanghai's wharves, there are hardly any that are equipped with light railways, and the mechanical equipment such as cranes is also very lacking. Other equipment such as barges and warehouses is also not perfect. In short, if we want to develop Shanghai and China's foreign trade, it is necessary to improve the wharves. This is undeniable.

The Qujiang Wharf, which started construction last May, is a unique color in the history of China's commercial ports. The wharf will be completed this year. Its nature, equipment, management, and location are all very perfect. It deserves to be the largest wharf in China. In the future, it will have great benefits for the prosperity of Shanghai and the development of China's international trade. From the perspective of foreign trade, the characteristics of Qujiang Wharf are approximately six points:

1. Qujiang Wharf is the largest state-owned wharf in China. Qujiang Wharf is operated by the Central Bank, so Qujiang Wharf is not only a wharf operated by China, but also a state-owned wharf in China. Since the wharf is state-owned, its purpose is purely to promote the prosperity of commercial ports and trade, and not to seek profit for itself. Therefore, not only will its fees be lower than other wharves, but it will also be able to provide various new-style wharf equipment to facilitate the loading and unloading of commercial goods. What private wharves cannot do, Qujiang Wharf can advocate and do.

2. Qujiang Wharf is Shanghai's largest wharf with a wide surface and deep water. Due to waterway conditions, most of Shanghai's wharves must wait for the tide for large ships to enter and exit. Qujiang Wharf is located at the mouth of the Qujiang River, with a straight shoreline, the widest surface, and the deepest water. Any large ship can enter and exit without waiting for the tide, and can avoid various dangers and berth safely. Time and expenses can be saved, and efficiency can be improved.

3. Qujiang Wharf is the wharf with the best location. Qujiang Wharf is located at the mouth of the Qujiang River in Yinhang District, Shanghai, facing the Huangpu River and connecting to the city center in the west, close to the industrial and commercial area in Shanghai's plan. In the future, as the city center becomes more and more developed and the Greater Shanghai Plan is gradually completed, the wharf will undoubtedly become the outlet of the city center. The main principle of wharf construction is that its location must not only meet current needs, but also adapt to future development. Qujiang Wharf has both. Therefore, when the engineering experts of the League of Nations inspected Shanghai's commercial port in 1932, they also believed that the mouth of the Qujiang River was close to the new urban area and was an ideal location for building mail ships and other commercial vessel wharves.

4. Qujiang Wharf is the wharf with the most complete equipment in China. Qujiang Wharf currently has two steel-framed concrete wharves, each 590 meters long, which can berth the largest giant ships in the world coming to Shanghai. Between the two wharves, there is a barge port, where barges of all sizes are berthed. On the wharf, there are two warehouses and two iron-shed flat warehouses, which can accommodate a total of 15,000 tons of goods. In the two warehouses, various offices and rest rooms are built. Qujiang Wharf is the first in Shanghai to have offices in the wharf. Outside the warehouse, there are several extra-large cranes installed. Heavy goods in the ship can be lifted by the crane to any floor of the warehouse, and goods in the warehouse can also be lifted to the cargo ship, without the need for workers to carry them, and the loading and unloading is very fast. This type of crane is an innovation in this port. In addition, light railways are laid in front and behind the warehouse to directly transport goods to cargo trucks, and then transfer them to various inland areas. This equipment is also unprecedented in Shanghai.

5. Qujiang Wharf has many transportation routes and convenient transportation. Whether a wharf can prosper largely depends on whether the hinterland is rich and deep. The size of the hinterland behind the wharf always depends on the number of transportation routes connecting the hinterland to the wharf. The more transportation routes, the faster the transportation and the lower the cost. Qujiang Wharf is located in front of the city center, not only is it most closely connected to the city center, but also the transportation to the special zone is extremely convenient. It takes less than ten minutes from the special zone to the wharf. In addition, the wharf also plans to lay three railway lines behind the warehouse to connect to the Songhu Road, and can implement intermodal transportation with the Beijing-Zhejiang-Jiangxi, Pingjin, and Longhai lines. Goods can be intermodally transported to various places without the need for warehouses. In terms of water transportation, the wharf can also directly unload and load ships sailing to various ports on the river and sea. Whether it is waterway or land route, it is very convenient, and it can greatly save time and expenses. In the future, the wharf will become one of the most convenient wharves for loading and unloading goods in China, which can be expected.

6. Qujiang Wharf is the wharf that can best adapt to future development. Now is the era of world economy, and business development is advancing rapidly. Shanghai is a commercial center in the Pacific Ocean, and its future development is unlimited. Therefore, wharf equipment should also be prepared to expand at any time to meet future needs, so as to maintain permanent prosperity. The area of Qujiang Wharf is more than 1,100 mu, and the land currently used is only one-third. There is a lot of remaining land, and there is no problem for future development. In terms of wharf construction, the current two wharves total 1,180 meters, which can berth two giant ships of more than 500 meters. The second planned step in the future is to extend the wharf to 3,000 meters, and at the same time can accommodate six giant ships of more than 500 meters in the world. There are currently two warehouses, and it is planned to build eight in the future. It is also planned to build three iron-shed flat warehouses. In addition, it is also planned to build travel agencies, shipping companies, transportation companies, and hotels, etc., in order to fully provide merchants with various conveniences.

The six characteristics of Qujiang Wharf listed above are closely related to the prosperity of China's international trade. In the future, when the wharf is completed, China's commercial transportation will become more and more convenient. It is expected that Shanghai and China's foreign trade will receive a new boost due to the completion of Qujiang Wharf. This is what we can assert when the foundation laying ceremony of Qujiang Wharf is held.

Shen Bao Women's Special

Beware of Traps 232

— Chen Danxing

Every dark corner of this society is filled with traps. Young women whose youthful fires are burning brightly and experiencing sexual impulses are no different from standing at the mouth of a bottomless trap. This is the most dangerous period of a woman's life, and it determines whether her entire future will be fortunate or unfortunate. It is like sailing a boat on a stormy sea. If you can have your own opinions, have perseverance, and hold the rudder steady, you can avoid danger and create a bright and happy future. If you are confused by a kind of wonderful temptation, unable to restrain the burning boredom of youth, "one wrong step brings everlasting regret." Precious youth and chastity will inevitably be swallowed up by beasts in human skin.

In every situation in this society, there are many such people in human skin with beastly hearts who feed on the youth and chastity of women. They have handsome appearances, speak sweet words, and have agile wrists. They set up traps and nets, waiting for young women who are just maturing, have weak wills, and have little life experience to fall into them. Don't we see lawsuits involving the loss of chastity in the social news in newspapers every day! There are many young women whose minds and bodies have been defiled because they have been deceived by others, but they dare not publicly announce it and file a lawsuit because it concerns their face and reputation. They still live in secret pain, destroying the courage to move forward. There are even more who are unknown. Whether they are intellectual, semi-civilized, or completely uneducated women, they must be vigilant. If they are driven by temporary feelings and resolutely embark on the road of "love," and the crime is committed and the tragic result begins, it is "too late to regret."

Socializing and love are not products of sin, if they can be obtained in a legitimate way without blindly following others. However, how many men and women in this society truly understand the true value and true meaning of socializing and love? Many women are groping on rugged roads with their eyes covered by vanity. Many women, at the peak of their burning youthful fires, have their entire nerves completely occupied by impulsive feelings. Therefore, they blindly hope to find an object in the form of "socializing." At this time, it is the best opportunity for a group of playboy men to set traps. Young women, beware of traps!

Do Women Need to Return to the Home? 233

— Shou Zhen

Ever since Xi Shiqin proposed the slogan of women returning to the home, a group of male chauvinists in male society immediately seemed to have obtained a kind of guarantee for their opinions. They loudly raised many unreasonable arguments against the women's movement, women's participation in politics, and women's activities in the workplace. They wanted to take advantage of this trend to drive the women who had just begun to show their faces in society back to the home and suppress the women who were preparing to raise their sails to society in the dark corners of the home, in order to protect their male-centered social bulwark.

Originally, in China, the social status of women was already pitiful enough. Although the women's movement, following the upsurge of the May Fourth Movement, had once obtained the government's recognition of the equality of women's social status in politics, economics, education, and all other areas, it only raised the status of a very, very small number of privileged women, as a superficial perfunctory measure. In reality, the vast majority of women are still suffocated in the kitchen, and have never seen a glimmer of light. Now, the big men and gentlemen of China are actually learning the fashion and calling for women to return to the home. In fact, they have not seen that Chinese women do not need to be so worried.

Now, standing on the position of human beings, let us calmly discuss whether women, in addition to housework, cannot participate in other career activities? Of course, the family is the foundation of society, and we cannot abandon the family because of social work. However, this responsibility is not for women alone but for both men and women. If men, under the guise of working in society, completely unload the responsibility of the family and simply send a little money home every month, then for the so-called wife, it is completely like hiring an employee. Then why can't the woman go to society to earn money to hire a man or other women who do this as a profession to maintain her family for her? Therefore, this situation can never make women succumb.

In general, people always think that women's nature is suitable for managing the home, so women should be in the home. This is also not a reason at all. If women were not restrained by thousands of years of ritual education and the pure family environment, and had been cultivated to be so weak and incompetent from childhood, it is not certain that they would not be strong, brave, and very capable. We can understand this clearly by comparing the labor situation of women in border areas where the culture is relatively backward and the power of ritual education is relatively weak. Moreover, in fact, among the general women today, there are many women who are strong and capable enough to assume social work and the great responsibilities of mankind. On the contrary, among men, there are many who are incompetent and only know how to spend money on drinking and entertainment, without engaging in production.

Moreover, we Chinese have always suppressed women in the home. No matter how much a job needs people, they are always unwilling to realize that capable women can help, and would rather have a general incompetent man to muddle through, resulting in the social undertaking as a whole declining day by day. Also, because there are few producers and many consumers, every family feels economic panic, forming a weak economic force for the entire society. Therefore, Chinese women, in theory, especially need to come out to work in society.

Therefore, in my personal opinion, if a woman's ability and ambition are sufficient to achieve a career, then of course she should contribute her ability to society and compete with society. If a woman's strength is sufficient to manage the home and there is still extra strength, then in addition to managing the home, she should also use her spare strength to serve society. Furthermore, if a woman's temperament is indeed gentle and indecisive, and she is not interested in social undertakings, then she might as well settle down in the home. The so-called slogan of women returning to the home is fundamentally unreasonable and not applicable to China.

Now, for the capable and knowledgeable women who are living at home, I hope that you will come to society. Indeed, modern China needs the strength of the entire nation!

So-Called Wonderful Beauty Methods 234

— Da Qian

Women's love of beauty is in their nature and is also a virtue. In the past, the methods of embellishment were not sophisticated. When beauty faded or was not endowed at birth, one could only lament at the mirror. In modern times, all kinds of surgeries are available, so there are so-called wonderful beauty methods. Paris has a doctor named Fassot, who is the world's most famous expert in facial modification. Since his death (he recently passed away), the beauty methods he used have become the wonderful techniques of "facial doctors" everywhere. In recent years, "beauty salons" have appeared in the United States, taking advantage of the trend of the times and catering to the preferences of women. Can such organizations avoid not spreading to our country without being asked? What is the matter in the end? It is not enough to draw a conclusion without knowing its contents. This is the reason why this article was written.

The currently popular beauty and body methods include the following types, and their results are described separately below:

Wrinkle Removal Method When people reach old age, their blood is insufficient, and wrinkles naturally appear on their faces. This is the same reason why oranges wrinkle when they are left for too long and the water evaporates. The wonderful wrinkle removal method used by beauticians is not to fill in the wrinkles and moisturize the dryness, but to cut off a part of the loose and wrinkled skin. The method is to choose the end of the hair behind the ear (the edge of the hair behind the curved ear), make a small incision with a knife, and tightly pull the skin of the face until there are no wrinkles. Then, the loose and excess skin is cut off and sewn with thread. The sewing place is on the edge of the hair, and it is not easy for people to find it by using the cover of the hair. However, if you are a little careless when getting a haircut, and the barber cuts it too short, there is a risk of the truth coming out. One day in the United States, a woman came to a barber shop and angrily negotiated with the barber why he had cut her hair too short, so that she could not go out to see people. The barber did not understand at first, but later he knew that the reason for offending her was that the crux of the problem was exposed. After this method is performed, wrinkles will reappear on the face after a short period of time, and it must be pulled and cut again. After several pulls and cuts, the face will lose its original appearance, and it is very likely that the eyes will become deformed. Seeking beauty will instead help ugliness!

Skin Rejuvenation Method The skin rejuvenation method is to remove the dry and withered epidermis and make it become tender skin. The method currently used by beauticians is: (A) Mix dry soil with water to form a thick slurry, apply it to the skin, and peel it off after it is dry and hard; (B) Melt wax into a slurry, apply it to the skin, and peel it off after it is cooled and solidified; (C) Pound water plants and called-for materials into a slurry, apply it to the skin, and peel it off after it is dry. During the period from applying the slurry to peeling it off, all of the above methods have extremely unbearable discomforts, especially the heat of the wax, which is like burning. The result is that the tender skin obtained by all of the above methods lasts for only a few hours.

Hair Perming The burning of hair during perming has been repeatedly heard in our country. It is not only dangerous to perm your own hair, but it is also inevitable in barber shops. The permed hair in barber shops in our country also has the regret that it will still return to its original shape after being washed with hot water and cannot last. The art of hair perming is developed in the United States. The so-called permanent waves can indeed last unchanged. The wage rate must be several US dollars. What women often complain about is not the too much cost, but the pain of perming. This kind of perming uses a perming machine, and the woman's hair must be twisted on the perming machine, and then it is oiled and permed. The beautiful women of the time, those who joked about it likened it to the Yasha, the truth is probably not far from it! After several hours of baking, the work can be completed, but the beauty that can be enjoyed is only a few months! (Generally three or four months) After a few months, the permed part will be gradually cut off because it is long, and the new part will replace it, and then it will have to suffer ten times the pain!

Looking at the above-mentioned various beauty methods, they all have great pain. There was a woman in the United States who came out of the beauty salon, and someone asked her how the taste of beauty was. The woman answered immediately: "Oh my god! Wonderful beauty method!" In this cry of "Oh my god", the kind of thing she suffered can be imagined! As for whether the so-called beauty must be found in embellishment, it is a matter of opinion.

Family Budget Issues 235

— Xian

State organs must have budgets, commercial organs must have budgets, and families naturally need to have budgets as well. Establishing a budget in a family is really a very meaningful thing, because with a budget, although it is not possible to spend every penny according to the rational budget, and it can be completely suitable for the ideal spending, but to some extent, it can always reduce some of the imbalances in income and expenditure because there is a budget. However, in our country's families, there are also many who have established a budget that could not be more reasonable at the beginning of the year, but as a result, expenditures often far exceed income and they incur a lot of debt. The crux of the problem is naturally quite complicated, but I think the most appropriate explanation is no better than the speech given by Mrs. Mary Ful on the subject of "Family Budget Issues" at a women's and family club in London in February of this year.

The topic of her speech was "Family Budget Issues." She said that having a budget in a family can indicate that there must be a thrifty, careful, and responsible housewife in this family. Moreover, it is very easy to prepare a budget in every family. For example, purchase a diary for the coming year on Christmas. Once the diary is purchased, you should record what you have done every day. This matter will test whether the person who prepared the diary has perseverance. The same is true for the family budget. Once the budget is made, you should prepare a record book of income and expenditure and record all income and expenditure item by item every day, and it should be classified page by page. For example, the first page is exclusively for food accounts, the second page is exclusively for clothing accounts, the third page is exclusively for book and magazine accounts, and the fourth page is exclusively for medical expenses. This kind of account seems to be very cumbersome, but from these cumbersome pages, it is easy to compare the income and expenditure situation with the budget and reflect on whether life is reasonable. When a considerable period of time expires (assuming it is one year), then, from the totals of each special page, the difference from the budget can be compared. This kind of perseverance in bookkeeping is not without reward. The final account for the first year is a model for preparing the budget for the second year. In other words, it is a family issue of the obligatory family advisor for the second year. Anyone in the entire family can rationally relax and tighten their lives according to the guidance of this obligatory family consultant in order to suit the balance of income and expenditure and avoid the pain of debt. The matter of debt is an evil spirit that destroys happy families and plunders family happiness, but a thrifty, careful, and responsible housewife in the family can very persistently prepare a reasonable budget, balance the family's income and expenditure, and solve all the problems that are not easy to solve in ordinary families.

I have several friends whose families do not have a budget and do not have daily records of income and expenditure. At the end of the year, some have worked hard for a year but have no surplus funds, and some have simply incurred a lot of debts. As a result, the husband complains about the wife's mismanagement of the home, and even insults the wife for making secret savings or spending unjustifiable money. Naturally, in order to avoid their own responsibility, the wives have to attack the husband's weaknesses in a far-fetched way, and become like fire and water to each other. Is this kind of problem impossible to solve? When we look at Mrs. Mary Ful's speech on "Family Budget Issues," we feel that it is not difficult to solve this problem. It is only necessary for the housewife in each family to spare a quarter of an hour of time every day to record a few accounts of vegetables and tofu, and write black ink on white paper. Husbands for wives, wives for husbands, everyone can no longer blame each other, and perhaps because of this practical record, they can learn from each other's strengths and make up for each other's weaknesses, so as to avoid the imbalance of income and expenditure in the next year and establish a reasonable family expenditure system, a budget, as a guideline for life.

Regarding Human Milk Nutrition 237

— Zhang Yuxiu

Breast milk is a natural nutrient for infants. Breastfeeding infants not only saves time but is also economical. However, due to various reasons, mothers often do not want to breastfeed themselves and mostly hire wet nurses; some also use cow's milk or formula. These inevitably have shortcomings. If the mother cannot breastfeed due to special physical reasons or illnesses, it is forgivable. However, what is commonly seen is that most modern housewives are afraid that breastfeeding will damage their beauty or hinder their social life, so they are unwilling to use their own milk to feed their lovely infants. As a result, their children fall into very pitiful circumstances. Generally, people know that the health of the human body is closely related to the nutrition of milk in childhood. I am now writing down the benefits of breastfeeding and the harms of wet nursing or artificial feeding to give a loyal warning to those who do not have diseases but are unwilling to breastfeed.

The Value of Breast Milk Nutrition

The value of breast milk nutrition Breastfeeding has the following benefits: Contains special vitamins, Contains special immunity, Suitable temperature, Because it does not pass through utensils, bacteria cannot enter, Is a natural beverage for infants. Therefore, to make children healthy, it is best to breastfeed them with breast milk. Except for those who have lung disease, heart disease, acute nephritis, or acute infectious diseases, etc., and cannot breastfeed, the rest should all breastfeed themselves. Even mothers who are thin and weak, many doctors also encourage them to breastfeed themselves. (Because during the breastfeeding period, the appetite can increase, and the nutrition they take in, in addition to providing milk, often has a surplus, or they may even become fat and strong as a result.) If the mother has syphilis, she should breastfeed herself even more. Because syphilis is hereditary, the infant is infected early when it is born. If such infants are fed artificially, nutritional disorders are likely to occur. If a wet nurse is hired, syphilis can be transmitted from the infant to the wet nurse. Therefore, it is better for the mother to breastfeed herself, and both parties will be fine. Asia has wet nursing, and if their working hours are from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM in the morning and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM in the afternoon, then wet nursing is not a problem. Because the mother can breastfeed when she goes home for lunch, she can breastfeed when she has not gone to work in the morning, and she can also breastfeed when she goes home in the evening. If the working hours are special, she can also find a way to breastfeed herself. In addition, if the mother's milk is scarce, artificial milk substitutes can be added, but breastfeeding should never be stopped. Mother's breastfeeding is not only of great benefit to the infant, but also of many benefits to the mother, such as breastfeeding the infant when it is first born can make the mother's uterus quickly return to its original position, reducing the suffering of back pain and backache in the future. This can be verified.

Review of Hiring Wet Nurses to Breastfeed

Because women's occupations are not developed and the standard of living is relatively low in China, hiring wet nurses is not difficult. In other countries, the development of women's occupations and the increase in the standard of living make it simply difficult to hire wet nurses. Moreover, from a moral point of view, hiring wet nurses is also inappropriate, because the wet nurse's infant loses breast milk and changes to an unsuitable milk substitute, which often leads to illness and death. Let us think about it, the wet nurse sacrifices the life of her own biological child to exchange for a small amount of money, and the general healthy housewife is unwilling to breastfeed herself, which violates humanity. Furthermore, breastfeeding also has a nervous relationship. Most wet nurses are uneducated. After the infant grows up, its wisdom, temperament, and habits are like those of an uneducated wet nurse. Smart and clever mothers! You may not even know why you got such a child! In addition, wet nurses often use deceptive means for their little masters, such as immediately giving them milk when the little masters cry, etc., which is more likely to develop strange temperaments in infants. Therefore, except in cases of necessity, those with healthy mothers should always try to breastfeed themselves.

Special Article of this Newspaper

Ms. Lu Lihua Discusses the Current Situation of Women 238

— Ji Ping

Chinese people are already suffering enough, and women suffer even more than men. For women who strive to work for society, the current environment is truly extraordinarily difficult... These few sentences are the experienced words of Ms. Lu Lihua. Ms. Lu has been managing women's sports for seventeen years. She has tasted all kinds of sweetness, sourness, bitterness, and spiciness in society, and is still able to calmly work hard. Frankly speaking, this spirit is indelible. A few days ago, she was returning from Hong Kong, and we ran into each other. We casually chatted and talked about women's issues. Her opinions are very sympathetic.

Cultivate Independence

For thousands of years, our country's deep-rooted habit of valuing men and belittling women has unreasonably oppressed women, and this has not been completely eradicated. In the past twenty years, women have made great efforts and have won legal status, but in reality, women are still subject to too many restrictions, and are far from the stage of equality. Currently, there are quite a few women in the country with knowledge and skills, but they are still unable to contribute all of their learning to society and the country, which is a great pity. According to today's situation, women should stand up, and the prerequisite must be a healthy body. Diligently seeking knowledge, strong will, and cultivating an independent spirit are also very important. In addition to women's own efforts, for gender equality, it is also hoped that men will respect women and take a supportive attitude at any time, just like adults supporting children learning to walk. If the inherent abilities of men and women reach a certain standard, I believe that small families will reduce their burden and increase happiness, and large societies will work together to build the country, with half the effort and twice the result, which is not an exaggeration.

General Shortcomings

Handling household affairs is originally the responsibility of women, but they should not only take care of family affairs and neglect social work. They should divide their remaining energy to serve the public. When it comes to managing a household, I advocate economical, rational, and artistic methods to improve past bad habits. Many housewives never tidy up their homes, and spend the whole day busy, suffering a lot, but from an objective point of view, it is still chaotic and disorganized. If they can apply scientific methods, the work of a day can be done in half a day. The biggest shortcomings of women are their short-sightedness, narrow-mindedness, and lack of a broad-minded and optimistic attitude. Therefore, at home, they often argue and turn against each other over trivial matters. When serving outside, they are wary of each other and cannot respect their work and enjoy being with others. Once others gossip, they shift their will and create troubles for themselves. These abnormal situations should be avoided as much as possible. The way of husband and wife should be based on equal treatment. If a man regards a woman as low-powered and has a sense of contempt, and a woman regards a man as all-powerful and develops a sense of dependence, the family will have no happiness. I believe that "respect" and "understanding" are the elements of love, not only for husband and wife, but also for dealing with people and things.

Women of the Far East

Ms. Lu has been to many places in the Far East, and I asked her to make a general criticism of women in various places. She said: "I only stayed for a short time in the places I went to, and did not have a deep understanding. I will try to describe what I saw. In the country, I feel that women in Jiangsu and Zhejiang have taken the lead in the civilized atmosphere, and their material enjoyment is better than other places, but they are gentle and timid. Women in Central China are quite brave, especially women in Hunan Province, who have a spirit of progress. Women in North China have the virtues of perseverance and hard work. Due to geographical reasons, South China is also the hub for overseas Chinese to enter and exit, and it is more deeply stimulated, and has more opportunities to imitate Westernization and participate in occupations, so the situation is different from other places. For example, the training of professional women in Hong Kong and Guangdong is comparable to that of Japan. I have carefully observed them and firmly believe that they can respect themselves and serve for the sake of service. In foreign countries, Japanese women are extremely docile and hard-working, and they have quite a powerful force in the workplace. Women's groups have very strong organizations, but they rely on men for everything, and their civic personality is relatively low. I traveled to Korea five years ago, and the scene of national subjugation was very tragic! They have received slave education and have lost their national concept, so there is simply no women's issue to discuss. In the South Pacific Islands, such as the Philippines, women's education is very popular, and men and women are absolutely equal. Women's service efficiency is very high, and women's circles are also very connected. I visited the women's conference in the Philippines, which had more than fifty unit members, representing more than five thousand people. The atmosphere was vibrant and admirable. In the Dutch East Indies, women are especially respected. For example, if a woman hits a man, the man cannot sue, and vice versa, the man will be severely punished. It is said that Dutch society expresses respect for women everywhere, probably because of the Dutch Queen. Although the natives in the British and French territories are in a semi-civilized period, men and women seem to have complete equality."

Women and Sports

She also said that the reason why the women's issue has not been completely resolved so far is that sports are a major core issue. For this reason, I have sacrificed all my personal happiness, working hard and bearing grievances, and taking the management of women's sports as a consistent policy. Looking back on the past seventeen years, I don't know how many setbacks I have encountered, but I have never been discouraged by difficulties. Fortunately, Chinese people have a considerable understanding of women's sports. From now on, I advocate that women's sports should not be limited to schools, but should be extended from schools to families and society, expand the implementation, and the effect will be great. Sports are multifaceted and have mutually related relationships with medicine and hygiene. When the three are integrated, people can enjoy healthy happiness. We must allocate the amount of sports to our daily life, and hope that women across the country will engage in sports, work hard in sports, create a strong atmosphere, and sweep away the weakness of women for thousands of years. By that time, the entire women's issue will be easily resolved.

The Error of Celibacy (Part 1) 239

— Yue Xin

—Dedicated to Sisters with Celibate Ideas—

The idea of celibacy is wrong: this is something everyone should admit. Why? The so-called "celibacy" is explained as not uniting with the opposite sex. We know that all living things mostly reproduce their seeds and prolong their lives through the union of two sexes. The individual life of a living thing is very short. If the previous ones die and the later ones do not grow, then there will be no living thing in the world, because a living thing cannot grasp eternal survival. Therefore, due to the natural union of the two sexes, a new life is born, and it continues day by day with the flow of time.

This is even more important for people: people are animals with two sexes by nature. They unite due to the needs of the two sexes, giving new impetus and reproducing the race. This is the innate instinct of mankind. However, humans are the most knowledgeable animals, and the union of the two sexes is not something they can choose at will. In the choice of the opposite sex, they often encounter many objective difficulties. Due to the occurrence of these difficulties, the so-called "celibacy" idea takes the opportunity to enter. However, there are many reasons for the origin of celibacy ideas, which can be roughly divided into the following categories:

(1) Suffering from heartbreak or marriage difficulties!

In our era of conflicting new and old ideas, and a society where capital and feudalism coexist, marriage is the most difficult problem to solve. Many women are buried in the difficulties of marriage. Although many women have strong personalities, they do not have the courage to break through the difficulties of reality. At this time, they suddenly discovered a path—the path of celibacy. They thought that this path would make them free and never suffer the pain of marriage again.

(2) In order to accomplish one's own career—

Some women often think that doing something must be without resistance, so that they can complete it without any hindrance. Therefore, they are too enthusiastic about their careers and ignore marriage. They feel that this is the only way to achieve their goals and develop themselves.

(3) Seeing through the world and thinking that life is nothing more than this—

Marriage and childbirth are such painful and troublesome things! Some single women must think this way. Their thoughts are close to decadence. They see the traces of pain in many women, and see many women commit suicide because of heartbreak, thinking that the opposite sex is a terrible thing. At the same time, they think that the joy and sorrow of life are completely empty things, so they feel that it is better to live a free and independent life alone.
